\item 
class \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_aa244002768af333ada868424b4c51ecd_aa244002768af333ada868424b4c51ecd}{QCPPolar\+Axis\+Angular}}
\end{DoxyCompactItemize}


\doxysubsection{Detailed Description}
The radial axis inside a radial plot. 

\begin{DoxyWarning}{Warning}
In this \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} version, polar plots are a tech preview. Expect documentation and functionality to be incomplete, as well as changing public interfaces in the future.
\end{DoxyWarning}
Each axis holds an instance of \doxylink{class_q_c_p_axis_ticker}{QCPAxis\+Ticker} which is used to generate the tick coordinates and tick labels. You can access the currently installed \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a0c38b1920e69759bcc733975d5fbe758_a0c38b1920e69759bcc733975d5fbe758}{ticker} or set a new one (possibly one of the specialized subclasses, or your own subclass) via \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_abaf4c7f55113ccacfb0db2154add4811_abaf4c7f55113ccacfb0db2154add4811}{set\+Ticker}. For details, see the documentation of \doxylink{class_q_c_p_axis_ticker}{QCPAxis\+Ticker}.

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_acd7247b9f2196e1053f236b950a13b60_acd7247b9f2196e1053f236b950a13b60} 
QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::\+QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{\mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_angular}{QCPPolar\+Axis\+Angular}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{parent}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [explicit]}}

Constructs an Axis instance of Type {\itshape type} for the axis rect {\itshape parent}.

Usually it isn\textquotesingle{}t necessary to instantiate axes directly, because you can let \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} create them for you with \doxylink{class_q_c_p_axis_rect_a2a845ee60eac7a8d5e71718c5e77c274_a2a845ee60eac7a8d5e71718c5e77c274}{QCPAxis\+Rect\+::add\+Axis}. If you want to use own QCPAxis-\/subclasses however, create them manually and then inject them also via \doxylink{class_q_c_p_axis_rect_a2a845ee60eac7a8d5e71718c5e77c274_a2a845ee60eac7a8d5e71718c5e77c274}{QCPAxis\+Rect\+::add\+Axis}. Here is the call graph for this function\+:\nopagebreak

\end{center}
\end{figure}

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a2020514253527e80000775ea994c73e4_a2020514253527e80000775ea994c73e4}\index{QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}!getPartAt@{getPartAt}}
\index{getPartAt@{getPartAt}!QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{getPartAt()}{getPartAt()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a2020514253527e80000775ea994c73e4_a2020514253527e80000775ea994c73e4} 
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_ad022e747b5fc6aeaa6ff3587eee22908_ad022e747b5fc6aeaa6ff3587eee22908}{QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::\+Selectable\+Part}} QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::get\+Part\+At (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const QPointF \&}]{pos}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const}

Returns the part of the axis that is hit by {\itshape pos} (in pixels). The return value of this function is independent of the user-\/selectable parts defined with \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_aa4b946a386a837a534625d63fe6658d2_aa4b946a386a837a534625d63fe6658d2}{set\+Selectable\+Parts}. Further, this function does not change the current selection state of the axis.

If the axis is not visible (\doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_a3bed99ddc396b48ce3ebfdc0418744f8_a3bed99ddc396b48ce3ebfdc0418744f8}{set\+Visible}), this function always returns \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_ad022e747b5fc6aeaa6ff3587eee22908_ad022e747b5fc6aeaa6ff3587eee22908a4f6e2acf66dbfb63325f8a54c9da4fe2}{sp\+None}.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_layerable_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81}\index{QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}!mouseDoubleClickEvent@{mouseDoubleClickEvent}}
\index{mouseDoubleClickEvent@{mouseDoubleClickEvent}!QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{mouseDoubleClickEvent()}{mouseDoubleClickEvent()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_layerable_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81} 
void QCPLayerable\+::mouse\+Double\+Click\+Event (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{QMouse\+Event \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{event}{, }\item[{const QVariant \&}]{details}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}, {\ttfamily [virtual]}, {\ttfamily [inherited]}}

This event gets called when the user presses the mouse button a second time in a double-\/click, while the cursor is over the layerable. Whether a cursor is over the layerable is decided by a preceding call to \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_afc641137eaf389f6a8490a3cf8131cb4_afc641137eaf389f6a8490a3cf8131cb4}{select\+Test}.

The \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81}{mouse\+Double\+Click\+Event} is called instead of the second \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88}{mouse\+Press\+Event}. So in the case of a double-\/click, the event succession is {\itshape press\+Event -- release\+Event -- double\+Click\+Event -- release\+Event}.

The current pixel position of the cursor on the \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} widget is accessible via {\ttfamily event-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}pos()}. The parameter {\itshape details} contains layerable-\/specific details about the hit, which were generated in the previous call to \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_afc641137eaf389f6a8490a3cf8131cb4_afc641137eaf389f6a8490a3cf8131cb4}{select\+Test}. For example, One-\/dimensional plottables like \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph}{QCPGraph} or \doxylink{class_q_c_p_bars}{QCPBars} convey the clicked data point in the {\itshape details} parameter, as \doxylink{class_q_c_p_data_selection}{QCPData\+Selection} packed as QVariant. Multi-\/part objects convey the specific {\ttfamily Selectable\+Part} that was hit (e.\+g. \doxylink{class_q_c_p_axis_abee4c7a54c468b1385dfce2c898b115f_abee4c7a54c468b1385dfce2c898b115f}{QCPAxis\+::\+Selectable\+Part} in the case of axes).

Similarly to \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88}{mouse\+Press\+Event}, once a layerable has accepted the \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81}{mouse\+Double\+Click\+Event}, it is considered the mouse grabber and will receive all following calls to \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_acaaca448f4599cc4d8b4d6a35f61e1e6_acaaca448f4599cc4d8b4d6a35f61e1e6}{mouse\+Move\+Event} and \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a4fbf24f4373f8a4a740ab83b53a22c85_a4fbf24f4373f8a4a740ab83b53a22c85}{mouse\+Release\+Event} for this mouse interaction (a "{}mouse interaction"{} in this context ends with the release).

The default implementation does nothing except explicitly ignoring the event with {\ttfamily event-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}ignore()}.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88}{mouse\+Press\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_acaaca448f4599cc4d8b4d6a35f61e1e6_acaaca448f4599cc4d8b4d6a35f61e1e6}{mouse\+Move\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a4fbf24f4373f8a4a740ab83b53a22c85_a4fbf24f4373f8a4a740ab83b53a22c85}{mouse\+Release\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_ab495743f9f7412a109af0b0065a7b9ae_ab495743f9f7412a109af0b0065a7b9ae}{wheel\+Event} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}


Reimplemented in \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_text_element_a2272ff775ab385f612e9fd39773de7c0_a2272ff775ab385f612e9fd39773de7c0}{QCPText\+Element}}.

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_acaaca448f4599cc4d8b4d6a35f61e1e6_acaaca448f4599cc4d8b4d6a35f61e1e6}\index{QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}!mouseMoveEvent@{mouseMoveEvent}}
\index{mouseMoveEvent@{mouseMoveEvent}!QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{mouseMoveEvent()}{mouseMoveEvent()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_acaaca448f4599cc4d8b4d6a35f61e1e6_acaaca448f4599cc4d8b4d6a35f61e1e6} 
void QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::mouse\+Move\+Event (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{QMouse\+Event \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{event}{, }\item[{const QPointF \&}]{start\+Pos}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}, {\ttfamily [virtual]}}

This event gets called when the user moves the mouse while holding a mouse button, after this layerable has become the mouse grabber by accepting the preceding \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88}{mouse\+Press\+Event}.

The current pixel position of the cursor on the \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} widget is accessible via {\ttfamily event-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}pos()}. The parameter {\itshape start\+Pos} indicates the position where the initial \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88}{mouse\+Press\+Event} occurred, that started the mouse interaction.

The default implementation does nothing.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88}{mouse\+Press\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a4fbf24f4373f8a4a740ab83b53a22c85_a4fbf24f4373f8a4a740ab83b53a22c85}{mouse\+Release\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81}{mouse\+Double\+Click\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_ab495743f9f7412a109af0b0065a7b9ae_ab495743f9f7412a109af0b0065a7b9ae}{wheel\+Event} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}


Reimplemented from \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_layerable_a9eee1ba47fd69be111059ca3881933e4_a9eee1ba47fd69be111059ca3881933e4}{QCPLayerable}}.

\index{mousePressEvent@{mousePressEvent}!QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{mousePressEvent()}{mousePressEvent()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88} 
void QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::mouse\+Press\+Event (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{QMouse\+Event \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{event}{, }\item[{const QVariant \&}]{details}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}, {\ttfamily [virtual]}}

This event gets called when the user presses a mouse button while the cursor is over the layerable. Whether a cursor is over the layerable is decided by a preceding call to \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_afc641137eaf389f6a8490a3cf8131cb4_afc641137eaf389f6a8490a3cf8131cb4}{select\+Test}.

The current pixel position of the cursor on the \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} widget is accessible via {\ttfamily event-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}pos()}. The parameter {\itshape details} contains layerable-\/specific details about the hit, which were generated in the previous call to \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_afc641137eaf389f6a8490a3cf8131cb4_afc641137eaf389f6a8490a3cf8131cb4}{select\+Test}. For example, One-\/dimensional plottables like \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph}{QCPGraph} or \doxylink{class_q_c_p_bars}{QCPBars} convey the clicked data point in the {\itshape details} parameter, as \doxylink{class_q_c_p_data_selection}{QCPData\+Selection} packed as QVariant. Multi-\/part objects convey the specific {\ttfamily Selectable\+Part} that was hit (e.\+g. \doxylink{class_q_c_p_axis_abee4c7a54c468b1385dfce2c898b115f_abee4c7a54c468b1385dfce2c898b115f}{QCPAxis\+::\+Selectable\+Part} in the case of axes).

\doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} uses an event propagation system that works the same as Qt\textquotesingle{}s system. If your layerable doesn\textquotesingle{}t reimplement the \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88}{mouse\+Press\+Event} or explicitly calls {\ttfamily event-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}ignore()} in its reimplementation, the event will be propagated to the next layerable in the stacking order.

Once a layerable has accepted the \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88}{mouse\+Press\+Event}, it is considered the mouse grabber and will receive all following calls to \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_acaaca448f4599cc4d8b4d6a35f61e1e6_acaaca448f4599cc4d8b4d6a35f61e1e6}{mouse\+Move\+Event} or \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a4fbf24f4373f8a4a740ab83b53a22c85_a4fbf24f4373f8a4a740ab83b53a22c85}{mouse\+Release\+Event} for this mouse interaction (a "{}mouse interaction"{} in this context ends with the release).

The default implementation does nothing except explicitly ignoring the event with {\ttfamily event-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}ignore()}.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_acaaca448f4599cc4d8b4d6a35f61e1e6_acaaca448f4599cc4d8b4d6a35f61e1e6}{mouse\+Move\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a4fbf24f4373f8a4a740ab83b53a22c85_a4fbf24f4373f8a4a740ab83b53a22c85}{mouse\+Release\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81}{mouse\+Double\+Click\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_ab495743f9f7412a109af0b0065a7b9ae_ab495743f9f7412a109af0b0065a7b9ae}{wheel\+Event} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a4fbf24f4373f8a4a740ab83b53a22c85_a4fbf24f4373f8a4a740ab83b53a22c85}\index{QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}!mouseReleaseEvent@{mouseReleaseEvent}}
\index{mouseReleaseEvent@{mouseReleaseEvent}!QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{mouseReleaseEvent()}{mouseReleaseEvent()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a4fbf24f4373f8a4a740ab83b53a22c85_a4fbf24f4373f8a4a740ab83b53a22c85} 
void QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::mouse\+Release\+Event (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{QMouse\+Event \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{event}{, }\item[{const QPointF \&}]{start\+Pos}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}, {\ttfamily [virtual]}}

This event gets called when the user releases the mouse button, after this layerable has become the mouse grabber by accepting the preceding \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88}{mouse\+Press\+Event}.

The current pixel position of the cursor on the \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} widget is accessible via {\ttfamily event-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}pos()}. The parameter {\itshape start\+Pos} indicates the position where the initial \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88}{mouse\+Press\+Event} occurred, that started the mouse interaction.

The default implementation does nothing.

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_accd47f3d0906649c04ec16b52f8f68bd_accd47f3d0906649c04ec16b52f8f68bd} 
void QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::move\+Range (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{double}]{diff}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

If the scale type (\doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_af307dd120363c58b915cbe255e8de588_af307dd120363c58b915cbe255e8de588}{set\+Scale\+Type}) is \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a2e208d6eac26cd5abecc075ff2e5e605_a2e208d6eac26cd5abecc075ff2e5e605ac3792de649afed8d8d70894d4e5497e9}{st\+Linear}, {\itshape diff} is added to the lower and upper bounds of the range. The range is simply moved by {\itshape diff}.

If the scale type is \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a2e208d6eac26cd5abecc075ff2e5e605_a2e208d6eac26cd5abecc075ff2e5e605a44fa891f769cd677cd2d3e3661ac0c39}{st\+Logarithmic}, the range bounds are multiplied by {\itshape diff}. This corresponds to an apparent "{}linear"{} move in logarithmic scaling by a distance of log(diff). Here is the call graph for this function\+:\nopagebreak

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{parentLayerable()}{parentLayerable()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_layerable_aa78b7e644d2c519e1a9a6f2ac5fcd858_aa78b7e644d2c519e1a9a6f2ac5fcd858} 
\mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_layerable}{QCPLayerable}} \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*} QCPLayerable\+::parent\+Layerable (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}, {\ttfamily [inherited]}}

Returns the parent layerable of this layerable. The parent layerable is used to provide visibility hierarchies in conjunction with the method \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_ab054e88f15d485defcb95e7376f119e7_ab054e88f15d485defcb95e7376f119e7}{real\+Visibility}. This way, layerables only get drawn if their parent layerables are visible, too.

Note that a parent layerable is not necessarily also the QObject parent for memory management. Further, a layerable doesn\textquotesingle{}t always have a parent layerable, so this function may return {\ttfamily nullptr}.

A parent layerable is set implicitly when placed inside layout elements and doesn\textquotesingle{}t need to be set manually by the user. Here is the caller graph for this function\+:\nopagebreak

\begin{center}

\end{center}
\end{figure}

const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_range}{QCPRange}} QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::range (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a648fe508359f88424bc40cded6a297a9_a648fe508359f88424bc40cded6a297a9}\index{QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}!rangeChanged@{rangeChanged}}
\index{rangeChanged@{rangeChanged}!QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{rangeChanged}{rangeChanged}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a648fe508359f88424bc40cded6a297a9_a648fe508359f88424bc40cded6a297a9} 
void QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::range\+Changed (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_range}{QCPRange}} \&}]{new\+Range}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [signal]}}

This signal is emitted when the range of this axis has changed. You can connect it to the \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a6a1ee54cda58cc96bd805b533ba081b0_a6a1ee54cda58cc96bd805b533ba081b0}{set\+Range} slot of another axis to communicate the new range to the other axis, in order for it to be synchronized.

You may also manipulate/correct the range with \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a6a1ee54cda58cc96bd805b533ba081b0_a6a1ee54cda58cc96bd805b533ba081b0}{set\+Range} in a slot connected to this signal. This is useful if for example a maximum range span shall not be exceeded, or if the lower/upper range shouldn\textquotesingle{}t go beyond certain values (see \doxylink{class_q_c_p_range_a22151e18d961d762d25721211e89c2e5_a22151e18d961d762d25721211e89c2e5}{QCPRange\+::bounded}). For example, the following slot would limit the x axis to ranges between 0 and 10\+: 
\begin{DoxyCode}{0}
\DoxyCodeLine{customPlot-\/>xAxis-\/>setRange(newRange.bounded(0,\ 10))}

\end{DoxyCode}

{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_layerable_ab054e88f15d485defcb95e7376f119e7_ab054e88f15d485defcb95e7376f119e7} 
bool QCPLayerable\+::real\+Visibility (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inherited]}}

Returns whether this layerable is visible, taking the visibility of the layerable parent and the visibility of this layerable\textquotesingle{}s layer into account. This is the method that is consulted to decide whether a layerable shall be drawn or not.

If this layerable has a direct layerable parent (usually set via hierarchies implemented in subclasses, like in the case of \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layout_element}{QCPLayout\+Element}), this function returns true only if this layerable has its visibility set to true and the parent layerable\textquotesingle{}s \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_ab054e88f15d485defcb95e7376f119e7_ab054e88f15d485defcb95e7376f119e7}{real\+Visibility} returns true. \Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a4448749008af786d15e806c956d022ee_a4448749008af786d15e806c956d022ee}\index{QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}!scaleRange@{scaleRange}}
\index{scaleRange@{scaleRange}!QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{scaleRange()}{scaleRange()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [1/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a4448749008af786d15e806c956d022ee_a4448749008af786d15e806c956d022ee} 
void QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::scale\+Range (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{double}]{factor}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Scales the range of this axis by {\itshape factor} around the center of the current axis range. For example, if {\itshape factor} is 2.\+0, then the axis range will double its size, and the point at the axis range center won\textquotesingle{}t have changed its position in the \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} widget (i.\+e. coordinates around the center will have moved symmetrically closer).

If you wish to scale around a different coordinate than the current axis range center, use the overload \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_aea527409448c9d000aa5de3d7eebd76a_aea527409448c9d000aa5de3d7eebd76a}{scale\+Range(double factor, double center)}. \end{center}
\end{figure}

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_aea527409448c9d000aa5de3d7eebd76a_aea527409448c9d000aa5de3d7eebd76a}\index{QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}!scaleRange@{scaleRange}}
\index{scaleRange@{scaleRange}!QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{scaleRange()}{scaleRange()}\hspace{0.1cm}{\footnotesize\ttfamily [2/2]}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_aea527409448c9d000aa5de3d7eebd76a_aea527409448c9d000aa5de3d7eebd76a} 
void QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::scale\+Range (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{double}]{factor}{, }\item[{double}]{center}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

This is an overloaded member function, provided for convenience. It differs from the above function only in what argument(s) it accepts.

Scales the range of this axis by {\itshape factor} around the coordinate {\itshape center}. For example, if {\itshape factor} is 2.\+0, {\itshape center} is 1.\+0, then the axis range will double its size, and the point at coordinate 1.\+0 won\textquotesingle{}t have changed its position in the \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} widget (i.\+e. coordinates around 1.\+0 will have moved symmetrically closer to 1.\+0).

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{selectionChanged}{selectionChanged}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a5529ef54d68219392e7baa64a9303bf2_a5529ef54d68219392e7baa64a9303bf2}

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_afc641137eaf389f6a8490a3cf8131cb4_afc641137eaf389f6a8490a3cf8131cb4}\index{QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}!selectTest@{selectTest}}
\index{selectTest@{selectTest}!QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{selectTest()}{selectTest()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_afc641137eaf389f6a8490a3cf8131cb4_afc641137eaf389f6a8490a3cf8131cb4} 
double QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::select\+Test (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const QPointF \&}]{pos}{, }\item[{bool}]{only\+Selectable}{, }\item[{QVariant \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{details}{ = {\ttfamily 0}}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [virtual]}}

This function is used to decide whether a click hits a layerable object or not.

{\itshape pos} is a point in pixel coordinates on the \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} surface. This function returns the shortest pixel distance of this point to the object. If the object is either invisible or the distance couldn\textquotesingle{}t be determined, -\/1.\+0 is returned. Further, if {\itshape only\+Selectable} is true and the object is not selectable, -\/1.\+0 is returned, too.

If the object is represented not by single lines but by an area like a \doxylink{class_q_c_p_item_text}{QCPItem\+Text} or the bars of a \doxylink{class_q_c_p_bars}{QCPBars} plottable, a click inside the area should also be considered a hit. In these cases this function thus returns a constant value greater zero but still below the parent plot\textquotesingle{}s selection tolerance. (typically the selection\+Tolerance multiplied by 0.\+99).

Providing a constant value for area objects allows selecting line objects even when they are obscured by such area objects, by clicking close to the lines (i.\+e. closer than 0.\+99\texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}selection\+Tolerance).

The actual setting of the selection state is not done by this function. This is handled by the parent \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} when the mouse\+Release\+Event occurs, and the finally selected object is notified via the select\+Event/ deselect\+Event methods.

{\itshape details} is an optional output parameter. Every layerable subclass may place any information in {\itshape details}. This information will be passed to \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a2e034f1262cb3a094e28dbd2df12dcf9_a2e034f1262cb3a094e28dbd2df12dcf9}{select\+Event} when the parent \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} decides on the basis of this select\+Test call, that the object was successfully selected. The subsequent call to \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a2e034f1262cb3a094e28dbd2df12dcf9_a2e034f1262cb3a094e28dbd2df12dcf9}{select\+Event} will carry the {\itshape details}. This is useful for multi-\/part objects (like \doxylink{class_q_c_p_axis}{QCPAxis}). This way, a possibly complex calculation to decide which part was clicked is only done once in \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_afc641137eaf389f6a8490a3cf8131cb4_afc641137eaf389f6a8490a3cf8131cb4}{select\+Test}. The result (i.\+e. the actually clicked part) can then be placed in {\itshape details}. So in the subsequent \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a2e034f1262cb3a094e28dbd2df12dcf9_a2e034f1262cb3a094e28dbd2df12dcf9}{select\+Event}, the decision which part was selected doesn\textquotesingle{}t have to be done a second time for a single selection operation.

In the case of 1D Plottables (\doxylink{class_q_c_p_abstract_plottable1_d}{QCPAbstract\+Plottable1D}, like \doxylink{class_q_c_p_graph}{QCPGraph} or \doxylink{class_q_c_p_bars}{QCPBars}) {\itshape details} will be set to a \doxylink{class_q_c_p_data_selection}{QCPData\+Selection}, describing the closest data point to {\itshape pos}.

You may pass {\ttfamily nullptr} as {\itshape details} to indicate that you are not interested in those selection details.

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a1466025a71161cba79964aa8ad34f3c4_a1466025a71161cba79964aa8ad34f3c4}\index{QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}!setNumberFormat@{setNumberFormat}}
\index{setNumberFormat@{setNumberFormat}!QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setNumberFormat()}{setNumberFormat()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a1466025a71161cba79964aa8ad34f3c4_a1466025a71161cba79964aa8ad34f3c4} 
void QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::set\+Number\+Format (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const QString \&}]{format\+Code}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Sets the number format for the numbers in tick labels. This {\itshape format\+Code} is an extended version of the format code used e.\+g. by QString\+::number() and QLocale\+::to\+String(). For reference about that, see the "{}\+Argument Formats"{} section in the detailed description of the QString class.

{\itshape format\+Code} is a string of one, two or three characters. The first character is identical to the normal format code used by Qt. In short, this means\+: \textquotesingle{}e\textquotesingle{}/\textquotesingle{}E\textquotesingle{} scientific format, \textquotesingle{}f\textquotesingle{} fixed format, \textquotesingle{}g\textquotesingle{}/\textquotesingle{}G\textquotesingle{} scientific or fixed, whichever is shorter.

The second and third characters are optional and specific to \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot}\+:~\newline
If the first char was \textquotesingle{}e\textquotesingle{} or \textquotesingle{}g\textquotesingle{}, numbers are/might be displayed in the scientific format, e.\+g. "{}5.\+5e9"{}, which is ugly in a plot. So when the second char of {\itshape format\+Code} is set to \textquotesingle{}b\textquotesingle{} (for "{}beautiful"{}), those exponential numbers are formatted in a more natural way, i.\+e. "{}5.\+5 \mbox{[}multiplication sign\mbox{]} 10 \mbox{[}superscript\mbox{]} 9"{}. By default, the multiplication sign is a centered dot. If instead a cross should be shown (as is usual in the USA), the third char of {\itshape format\+Code} can be set to \textquotesingle{}c\textquotesingle{}. The inserted multiplication signs are the UTF-\/8 characters 215 (0x\+D7) for the cross and 183 (0x\+B7) for the dot.

Examples for {\itshape format\+Code\+:} \begin{DoxyItemize}
\item {\ttfamily g} normal format code behaviour. If number is small, fixed format is used, if number is large, normal scientific format is used \item {\ttfamily gb} If number is small, fixed format is used, if number is large, scientific format is used with beautifully typeset decimal powers and a dot as multiplication sign \item {\ttfamily ebc} All numbers are in scientific format with beautifully typeset decimal power and a cross as multiplication sign \item {\ttfamily fb} illegal format code, since fixed format doesn\textquotesingle{}t support (or need) beautifully typeset decimal powers. Format code will be reduced to \textquotesingle{}f\textquotesingle{}. \item {\ttfamily hello} illegal format code, since first char is not \textquotesingle{}e\textquotesingle{}, \textquotesingle{}E\textquotesingle{}, \textquotesingle{}f\textquotesingle{}, \textquotesingle{}g\textquotesingle{} or \textquotesingle{}G\textquotesingle{}. Current format code will not be changed. \end{DoxyItemize}

void QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::set\+Range (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{double}]{position}{, }\item[{double}]{size}{, }\item[{Qt\+::\+Alignment\+Flag}]{alignment}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

This is an overloaded member function, provided for convenience. It differs from the above function only in what argument(s) it accepts.

Sets the range of the axis.

The {\itshape position} coordinate indicates together with the {\itshape alignment} parameter, where the new range will be positioned. {\itshape size} defines the size of the new axis range. {\itshape alignment} may be Qt\+::\+Align\+Left, Qt\+::\+Align\+Right or Qt\+::\+Align\+Center. This will cause the left border, right border, or center of the range to be aligned with {\itshape position}. Any other values of {\itshape alignment} will default to Qt\+::\+Align\+Center. {\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_ad4fb4fb3d7f042267a32414c60cb0b78_ad4fb4fb3d7f042267a32414c60cb0b78} 
void QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::set\+Range\+Reversed (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{bool}]{reversed}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Sets whether the axis range (direction) is displayed reversed. Normally, the values on horizontal axes increase left to right, on vertical axes bottom to top. When {\itshape reversed} is set to true, the direction of increasing values is inverted.

Note that the range and data interface stays the same for reversed axes, e.\+g. the {\itshape lower} part of the \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a6a1ee54cda58cc96bd805b533ba081b0_a6a1ee54cda58cc96bd805b533ba081b0}{set\+Range} interface will still reference the mathematically smaller number than the {\itshape upper} part. \Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_ad7fea6680a0c0d0e7fddab06b5e03869_ad7fea6680a0c0d0e7fddab06b5e03869}\index{QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}!setRangeUpper@{setRangeUpper}}
\index{setRangeUpper@{setRangeUpper}!QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setRangeUpper()}{setRangeUpper()}}

Sets whether the axis uses a linear scale or a logarithmic scale.

Note that this method controls the coordinate transformation. For logarithmic scales, you will likely also want to use a logarithmic tick spacing and labeling, which can be achieved by setting the axis ticker to an instance of \doxylink{class_q_c_p_axis_ticker_log}{QCPAxis\+Ticker\+Log} \+:

\end{DoxyCodeInclude}

\index{setSelectedParts@{setSelectedParts}!QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setSelectedParts()}{setSelectedParts()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_af629128cb82825d6a550fb6f87130c25_af629128cb82825d6a550fb6f87130c25} 
void QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::set\+Selected\+Parts (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{const QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::\+Selectable\+Parts \&}]{selected\+Parts}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Sets the selected state of the respective axis parts described by \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_ad022e747b5fc6aeaa6ff3587eee22908_ad022e747b5fc6aeaa6ff3587eee22908}{Selectable\+Part}. When a part is selected, it uses a different pen/font.

The entire selection mechanism for axes is handled automatically when \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot_a5ee1e2f6ae27419deca53e75907c27e5_a5ee1e2f6ae27419deca53e75907c27e5}{QCustom\+Plot\+::set\+Interactions} contains i\+Select\+Axes. You only need to call this function when you wish to change the selection state manually.

This function can change the selection state of a part, independent of the \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_aa4b946a386a837a534625d63fe6658d2_aa4b946a386a837a534625d63fe6658d2}{set\+Selectable\+Parts} setting.

emits the \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a5529ef54d68219392e7baa64a9303bf2_a5529ef54d68219392e7baa64a9303bf2}{selection\+Changed} signal when {\itshape selected} is different from the previous selection state.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}

\index{setSubTickLength@{setSubTickLength}!QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setSubTickLength()}{setSubTickLength()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_ae3de39f6d88318769698aa035b1e194f_ae3de39f6d88318769698aa035b1e194f} 
void QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::set\+Sub\+Tick\+Length (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{int}]{inside}{, }\item[{int}]{outside}{ = {\ttfamily 0}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Sets the length of the subticks in pixels. {\itshape inside} is the length the subticks will reach inside the plot and {\itshape outside} is the length they will reach outside the plot. If {\itshape outside} is greater than zero, the tick labels and axis label will increase their distance to the axis accordingly, so they won\textquotesingle{}t collide with the ticks.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setSubTicks()}{setSubTicks()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a3a5628a92f5fe217c36afb2e9d0aaa7a_a3a5628a92f5fe217c36afb2e9d0aaa7a} 
void QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::set\+Sub\+Ticks (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{bool}]{show}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Sets whether sub tick marks are displayed.

Sub ticks are only potentially visible if (major) ticks are also visible (see \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a846d9220b5dd37072bd0ff89dab8e893_a846d9220b5dd37072bd0ff89dab8e893}{set\+Ticks})

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a846d9220b5dd37072bd0ff89dab8e893_a846d9220b5dd37072bd0ff89dab8e893}{set\+Ticks} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_abaf4c7f55113ccacfb0db2154add4811_abaf4c7f55113ccacfb0db2154add4811}\index{QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}!setTicker@{setTicker}}
\index{setTicker@{setTicker}!QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setTicker()}{setTicker()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_abaf4c7f55113ccacfb0db2154add4811_abaf4c7f55113ccacfb0db2154add4811} 
void QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::set\+Ticker (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{QShared\+Pointer$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_axis_ticker}{QCPAxis\+Ticker}} $>$}]{ticker}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

The axis ticker is responsible for generating the tick positions and tick labels. See the documentation of \doxylink{class_q_c_p_axis_ticker}{QCPAxis\+Ticker} for details on how to work with axis tickers.

You can change the tick positioning/labeling behaviour of this axis by setting a different \doxylink{class_q_c_p_axis_ticker}{QCPAxis\+Ticker} subclass using this method. If you only wish to modify the currently installed axis ticker, access it via \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a0c38b1920e69759bcc733975d5fbe758_a0c38b1920e69759bcc733975d5fbe758}{ticker}.

Since the ticker is stored in the axis as a shared pointer, multiple axes may share the same axis ticker simply by passing the same shared pointer to multiple axes.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}

\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setTickLabelRotation()}{setTickLabelRotation()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a68a064e85b5a807f8205e1996a50ebab_a68a064e85b5a807f8205e1996a50ebab} 
void QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::set\+Tick\+Label\+Rotation (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{double}]{degrees}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Sets the rotation of the tick labels. If {\itshape degrees} is zero, the labels are drawn normally. Else, the tick labels are drawn rotated by {\itshape degrees} clockwise. The specified angle is bound to values from -\/90 to 90 degrees.

If {\itshape degrees} is exactly -\/90, 0 or 90, the tick labels are centered on the tick coordinate. For other angles, the label is drawn with an offset such that it seems to point toward or away from the tick mark. Here is the call graph for this function\+:\nopagebreak

\begin{center}
\leavevmode

\end{center}
\end{figure}

\end{center}
\end{figure}

void QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::set\+Tick\+Labels (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{bool}]{show}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Sets whether tick labels are displayed. Tick labels are the numbers drawn next to tick marks. \Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a773447fe8c0031ee64ca6c5257778e11_a773447fe8c0031ee64ca6c5257778e11}\index{QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}!setTickLength@{setTickLength}}
\index{setTickLength@{setTickLength}!QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{setTickLength()}{setTickLength()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a773447fe8c0031ee64ca6c5257778e11_a773447fe8c0031ee64ca6c5257778e11} 
void QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::set\+Tick\+Length (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{int}]{inside}{, }\item[{int}]{outside}{ = {\ttfamily 0}}\end{DoxyParamCaption})}

Sets the length of the ticks in pixels. {\itshape inside} is the length the ticks will reach inside the plot and {\itshape outside} is the length they will reach outside the plot. If {\itshape outside} is greater than zero, the tick labels and axis label will increase their distance to the axis accordingly, so they won\textquotesingle{}t collide with the ticks.

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a0c6074d3c482a37187caffe8e2155f76_a0c6074d3c482a37187caffe8e2155f76}\index{QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}!subTickVector@{subTickVector}}

\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{subTickVector()}{subTickVector()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a0c6074d3c482a37187caffe8e2155f76_a0c6074d3c482a37187caffe8e2155f76} 
QVector$<$ double $>$ QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::sub\+Tick\+Vector (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a0c38b1920e69759bcc733975d5fbe758_a0c38b1920e69759bcc733975d5fbe758}\index{QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}!ticker@{ticker}}
\index{ticker@{ticker}!QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{ticker()}{ticker()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a0c38b1920e69759bcc733975d5fbe758_a0c38b1920e69759bcc733975d5fbe758} 
QShared\+Pointer$<$ \mbox{\hyperlink{class_q_c_p_axis_ticker}{QCPAxis\+Ticker}} $>$ QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::ticker (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}{}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption}) const\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [inline]}}

Returns a modifiable shared pointer to the currently installed axis ticker. The axis ticker is responsible for generating the tick positions and tick labels of this axis. You can access the \doxylink{class_q_c_p_axis_ticker}{QCPAxis\+Ticker} with this method and modify basic properties such as the approximate tick count (\doxylink{class_q_c_p_axis_ticker_a47752abba8293e6dc18491501ae34008_a47752abba8293e6dc18491501ae34008}{QCPAxis\+Ticker\+::set\+Tick\+Count}).

You can gain more control over the axis ticks by setting a different \doxylink{class_q_c_p_axis_ticker}{QCPAxis\+Ticker} subclass, see the documentation there. A new axis ticker can be set with \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_abaf4c7f55113ccacfb0db2154add4811_abaf4c7f55113ccacfb0db2154add4811}{set\+Ticker}.

Since the ticker is stored in the axis as a shared pointer, multiple axes may share the same axis ticker simply by passing the same shared pointer to multiple axes.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_abaf4c7f55113ccacfb0db2154add4811_abaf4c7f55113ccacfb0db2154add4811}{set\+Ticker} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}

\Hypertarget{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_ab495743f9f7412a109af0b0065a7b9ae_ab495743f9f7412a109af0b0065a7b9ae}\index{QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}!wheelEvent@{wheelEvent}}
\index{wheelEvent@{wheelEvent}!QCPPolarAxisRadial@{QCPPolarAxisRadial}}
\doxysubsubsection{\texorpdfstring{wheelEvent()}{wheelEvent()}}
{\footnotesize\ttfamily \label{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_ab495743f9f7412a109af0b0065a7b9ae_ab495743f9f7412a109af0b0065a7b9ae} 
void QCPPolar\+Axis\+Radial\+::wheel\+Event (\begin{DoxyParamCaption}\item[{QWheel\+Event \texorpdfstring{$\ast$}{*}}]{event}{}\end{DoxyParamCaption})\hspace{0.3cm}{\ttfamily [protected]}, {\ttfamily [virtual]}}

This event gets called when the user turns the mouse scroll wheel while the cursor is over the layerable. Whether a cursor is over the layerable is decided by a preceding call to \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_afc641137eaf389f6a8490a3cf8131cb4_afc641137eaf389f6a8490a3cf8131cb4}{select\+Test}.

The current pixel position of the cursor on the \doxylink{class_q_custom_plot}{QCustom\+Plot} widget is accessible via {\ttfamily event-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}pos()}.

The {\ttfamily event-\/\texorpdfstring{$>$}{>}angle\+Delta()} indicates how far the mouse wheel was turned, which is usually +/-\/ 120 for single rotation steps. However, if the mouse wheel is turned rapidly, multiple steps may accumulate to one event, making the delta larger. On the other hand, if the wheel has very smooth steps or none at all, the delta may be smaller.

The default implementation does nothing.

\begin{DoxySeeAlso}{See also}
\doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88_a0fa3d3c617a57b4115b9bec55b739f88}{mouse\+Press\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_acaaca448f4599cc4d8b4d6a35f61e1e6_acaaca448f4599cc4d8b4d6a35f61e1e6}{mouse\+Move\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_polar_axis_radial_a4fbf24f4373f8a4a740ab83b53a22c85_a4fbf24f4373f8a4a740ab83b53a22c85}{mouse\+Release\+Event}, \doxylink{class_q_c_p_layerable_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81_a4171e2e823aca242dd0279f00ed2de81}{mouse\+Double\+Click\+Event} 
\end{DoxySeeAlso}
